Nucleic Acids Res. 2003;31:36570." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1737">66</a>] with an <i>E</i> value cutoff of 1e5 used to assess orthology.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec18">Non-coding RNAs</h4><p>rDNA genes were identified by aligning with rRNA template sequences (Pfam database v22.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Finn RD, Bateman A, Clements J, Coggill P, Eberhardt RY, Eddy SR, Heger A, Hetherington K, Holm L, Mistry J, et al. Pfam: the protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 2014;42:D22230." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1751">67</a>], using BLAST [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Altschul SF, Gish W, Miller W, Myers EW, Lipman DJ. Basic local alignment search tool. J Mol Biol. 1990;215:40310." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1754">68</a>] with an <i>E</i> value of 1e10 and an identity cutoff of 95% or more. The tRNAScan-SE v2.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Lowe TM, Eddy SR. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 1997;25:95564." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1760">69</a>] algorithm with default parameters was applied to predict tRNA genes. miRNA genes were predicted using INFERNAL v1.1 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Nawrocki EP, Eddy SR. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics. 2013;29:29335." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1763">70</a>] with the Rfam database v11.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Griffiths-Jones S, Bateman A, Marshall M, Khanna A, Eddy SR. Rfam: an RNA family database. Nucleic Acids Res. 2003;31:43941." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1767">71</a>] and a cutoff score of 30 or more. The minimum cutoff score was based on the settings which yielded a false-positive rate of 30 bits.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Comparative analysis of gene families</h3><p>To identify homologous relationships among pistachio and related plants, the pistachio proteome was globally compared with the <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>C. sinensis</i>, <i>G. raimondii</i> (Phytozome v12.1), and <i>V. vinifera</i> (Phytozome v12.1) proteomes filtered for transposable elements and alternative splicing. An all-against-all comparison was performed using BLASTP (<i>E</i> value=1e5) followed by clustering with OrthoMCL v2.0.9 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Li L, Stoeckert CJ Jr, Roos DS. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 2003;13:217889." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1795">9</a>] (inflation = 1.5). Analysis of species-specific gene families was made with a Fishers exact test (<i>P</i>&lt;0.0001) on the Pfam domains.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Phylogenomic analysis</h3><p>A phylogenetic tree of 9 species<i>V. vinifera</i>, <i>Eucalyptus grandis</i> (Phytozome v12.1), <i>G. raimondii</i>, <i>Medicago sativa</i> (Phytozome v12.1), <i>Brassica rapa</i> (Phytozome v12.1), <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>P. trichocarpa</i> (<a href="http://ensemblgenomes.org">http://ensemblgenomes.org</a>,release-21), <i>C. sinensis</i>, and pistachiowas constructed using PhyML software v3.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Guindon S, Dufayard JF, Lefort V, Anisimova M, Hordijk W, Gascuel O. New algorithms and methods to estimate maximum-likelihood phylogenies: assessing the performance of PhyML 3.0. Syst Biol. 2010;59:30721." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1841">72</a>] based on 1096 shared single-copy genes. The divergence time between pistachio and the 8 other sequenced species (<i>V. vinifera</i> as the outgroup) was estimated using the MCMCtree program implemented in the PAML package v4.9 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Yang Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol Biol Evol. 2007;24:158691." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1848">73</a>]. Calibration times were obtained from the TimeTree database (<a href="http://www.timetree.org/">http://www.timetree.org/</a>). Expansion and contraction of OrthoMCL-derived gene clusters was determined by a CAF v2.1 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="De Bie T, Cristianini N, Demuth JP, Hahn MW. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics. 2006;22:126971." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1858">74</a>] calculation on the basis of changes in gene family size in the inferred phylogenetic history. KEGG and GO annotation of gene family was completed by aligning the genes to the KEGG database and NCBI non-redundant database using BlastP with an <i>E</i> value of 1e5, respectively. BLAST2GO [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Conesa A, Gotz S, Garcia-Gomez JM, Terol J, Talon M, Robles M. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics. 2005;21:36746." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1864">75</a>] was used to obtain the associated GO terms. The enrichment score is defined as the hypergeometric test value [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Goebels F, Frishman D. Prediction of protein interaction types based on sequence and network features. BMC Syst Biol. 2013;7(Suppl 6):S5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1867">76</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Whole genome duplication analysis</h3><p>The all-against-all BLASTP method (<i>E</i> value&lt;1e5) was used to detect paralogous genes in pistachio, <i>C. sinensis</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i>, and <i>P. trichocarpa</i> as well as orthologous genes in pistachio <i>C. sinensis</i> and pistachio <i>V. vinifera</i>. Homologous blocks were then detected using Mcscan v1.1 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Tang H, Bowers JE, Wang X, Ming R, Alam M, Paterson AH. Synteny and collinearity in plant genomes. Science. 2008;320:4868." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1897">77</a>]. The synonymous substitution (Ks) and fourfold degenerate site transversion (4DTV) values of the blocks were calculated using the HKY model [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Hasegawa M, Kishino H, Yano T. Dating of the human-ape splitting by a molecular clock of mitochondrial DNA. J Mol Evol. 1985;22:16074." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1900">78</a>].</p><p>Syntenic depth refers to the number of times a genomic region (or genome) is syntenic to the regions in another genome [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Ibarra-Laclette E, Lyons E, Hernandez-Guzman G, Perez-Torres CA, Carretero-Paulet L, Chang TH, Lan T, Welch AJ, Juarez MJ, Simpson J, et al. Architecture and evolution of a minute plant genome. Nature. 2013;498:948." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1906">79</a>]. We performed synteny searches to compare the pistachio genome structure with <i>A. trichopoda</i> (<i></i>-WGD [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Amborella Genome Project. The Amborella genome and the evolution of flowering plants. Science. 2013;342:1241089." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1915">7</a>]) (<a href="http://amborella.huck.psu.edu">http://amborella.huck.psu.edu</a>,version1.0) and <i>P. trichocarpa</i> (<i></i>-WGD, -WGD, and -WGD [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Tuskan GA, DiFazio S, Jansson S, Bohlmann J, Grigoriev I, Hellsten U, Putnam N, Ralph S, Rombauts S, Salamov A, et al. The genome of black cottonwood, Populus trichocarpa (Torr. &amp; Gray). Science. 2006;313:1596604." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1932">8</a>]) genomes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Salinity experiment</h3><p>A greenhouse experiment was conducted in 2016 at the Pistachio Research Center, Rafsanjan, Iran: 30 24 49.0 N, 55 59 20.8 E, at 1528masl. Seeds of cultivar pistachio rootstocks, <i>P. vera L. cv</i>. Ohadi, and the wild type (Sarakhs) were surface sterilized with 5% solution of sodium hypochlorite in distilled water and then incubated at 30C on a sterile moist cloth for 1&nbsp;week. Ten seeds that germinated were sown in each pot filled with about 7kg sandy-loam soil at a depth of about 2cm. The number of seedlings per pot was reduced to three uniform seedlings when the emergence period was completed about 3&nbsp;weeks of planting.</p><p>The experiment consisted of a completely randomized design with three replications for a total of six pots. Irrigation of all pots was carried out for 2months using Rafsanjan normal urban water (with a salinity of 0.6&nbsp;dS&nbsp;m<sup>1</sup>) at field capacity. Two months after planting, when seedlings were well established, salinity treatment was imposed on half of the pots (salinity group) by irrigation water with an electrical conductivity of 4.5&nbsp;dS&nbsp;m<sup>1</sup> while the other half of the pots (control group) were irrigated using the Rafsanjan normal urban water throughout the entire experiment. Salinity stress continued for 1&nbsp;month when the symptoms of salinity toxicity in the leaves (burning edge caused by salt toxicity) were observed. Leaf samples were taken before applying the salinity stress on the seedlings at 2&nbsp;months of age. Both the leaf and root samples from all replicates were taken at the end of the experiment when the seedlings were 3months of age. The fresh leaf and root tissue samples were immediately dissected and submerged in five volumes of RNA<i>later</i> solution and stored in a 80 freezer for subsequent RNA extraction. During the experiment, the maximum temperature was 345C; the minimum temperature was 214C, and the relative humidity was 405%.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">RNA sequencing</h3><p>The leaves and roots from the three salinity-treated samples of cultivar, three samples under control condition of cultivar, and three samples under control condition of wild were prepared for RNA sequencing. Total RNA was extracted using the RNAplant Plus Reagent according to the manufacturers instructions (Tiangen, Beijing, China). Before library construction, we evaluated the degradation of the RNA on a 1% agarose gel and checked the purity using the Qubit 3.0 Fluorometer (Life Technologies, CA, USA), with integrity and concentration assessed using an RNA Nano 6000 Assay Kit on the Bioanalyzer 2100 system (Agilent Technologies, CA, USA). Sequencing libraries were generated using NEBNext Ultra RNA Library Prep Kit for Illumina (#E7530L, NEB, USA) following the manufacturers recommendations and then sequenced on the Illumina HiSeq X Ten platform to generate 150bp paired-end reads.</p><p>Before alignment, reads were trimmed based on their quality scores using the quality trimming program Btrim [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Kong Y. Btrim: a fast, lightweight adapter and quality trimming program for next-generation sequencing technologies. Genomics. 2011;98:1523." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1967">80</a>]. Reads were aligned to our de novo genome of <i>Pistacia vera</i> L. using TopHat (v2.1.1 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Trapnell C, Roberts A, Goff L, Pertea G, Kim D, Kelley DR, Pimentel H, Salzberg SL, Rinn JL, Pachter L. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nat Protoc. 2012;7:562." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1973">18</a>]) and then assembled using Cufflinks (v2.2.1 with G parameter) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Trapnell C, Roberts A, Goff L, Pertea G, Kim D, Kelley DR, Pimentel H, Salzberg SL, Rinn JL, Pachter L. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nat Protoc. 2012;7:562." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1976">18</a>]. Differential expression of genes in the different tissues was calculated using Cuffdiff [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Trapnell C, Roberts A, Goff L, Pertea G, Kim D, Kelley DR, Pimentel H, Salzberg SL, Rinn JL, Pachter L. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nat Protoc. 2012;7:562." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d1768e1979">18</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Phenotyping</h3><p>Fruit size-related traits for pistachio were measured based on the pistachio descriptor (IPGRI. 1997. Descriptors for pistachio (<i>P. vera L.</i>), International Plant Genetic Resources Institute, Rome, Italy). The following phenotypes were recorded: dried pistachio fruit weight (gr) (the mean weight of 100 healthy dry nuts), fresh fruit weight with green skin (gr) (the mean weight of 100 healthy fresh nuts with green skin in grams), dried pistachio fruit length (mm) (average of 20 healthy nuts, measured from the most distant points along the main seed axis), dried pistachio fruit diameter (mm) (average of 20 healthy nuts, measured at the widest part perpendicular to the suture), dried pistachio fruit width (mm) (average of 20 healthy nuts, measured from the widest points perpendicular to the main seed axis), dried pistachio fruit and kernel shape (roundish = 1, ovoid = 2, elongated = 3, narrowly cordate = 4, cordate = 5), dried kernel weight (gr) (average weight of 100 healthy dry kernels), kernel diameter (mm) (average of 20 healthy kernels, measured at the widest part perpendicular to the cotyledon suture.), kernel width (mm) (average of 20 healthy kernels, measured on the widest points perpendicular to the main seed axis), kernel length (mm) (average of 20 healthy kernels, measured from the most distant points along the main seed axis).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Plant material and DNA extraction for genome resequencing</h3><p>Fresh leaves (45g) were sampled from the germplasm collections of the Pistachio Research Institute in Rafsanjan, Iran: 30 24 49.0 N, 55 59 20.8 E, at 1528masl; the pistachio germplasm of Ardakan, Iran: 32 18 36 N, 54 1 3 E, at 1040masl; and Jiroft, Iran: 28 40 41 N, 57 44 26 E, at 650masl. Leaf tissues were harvested during the 20152017 period and were transported on ice and stored at 80C in the Biotechnology Laboratory, Animal Science Department, Shahid Bahonar University of Kerman, Iran, until subjected to DNA extraction.</p><p>Total genomic DNA was extracted from 1g fresh leaves using hexadecyl trimethyl ammonium bromide (CTAB) protocol with some modifications. The quantity and quality of isolated DNA were assessed by NanoDrop spectrophotometer and 1% agarose gel electrophoresis, looking for a single absorbance peak at 260nm, a 260/280 absorbance ratio of 1.82.0, and no evidence of substantial band shearing or contamination. Extracted DNA was dissolved in 20l TE buffer (10mM Tris, pH 8, 1mM EDTA) and stored at 20C for subsequent NGS analysis.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Genome resequencing and SNP calling</h3><p>Among the above samples, 93 domestic and 14 wild pistachio individuals and another 13 <i>P. mutica</i>, 13 <i>P. khinjuk</i>, 4 <i>P. integerrima</i>, and 5 <i>P. palaestina</i> were chosen for genome resequencing. Ten micrograms of genomic DNA, prepared by the standard CTAB extraction protocol, was used to construct libraries with 350bp insert size. Sequence libraries were constructed according to the Illumina library preparation pipeline and were sequenced on the Illumina Hiseq 4000 platform to generate 150bp paired-end reads.</p><p>We mapped the reads to our reference genome (version 1) with BWA-MEM [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Li H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. arXiv. 2013;arXiv:1303.3997v2" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2028">81</a>]. After sorting and duplicate marking of the bam format files with Picards tools 1.56 (<a href="http://picard.sourceforge.net">http://picard.sourceforge.net</a>), we called SNPs using Genome Analysis Toolkit (GATK) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="McKenna A, Hanna M, Banks E, Sivachenko A, Cibulskis K, Kernytsky A, Garimella K, Altshuler D, Gabriel S, Daly M, DePristo MA. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 2010;20:1297303." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2038">28</a>]. The criteria used to filter the raw SNPs were QUAL &lt; 40.0, MQ &lt; 25.0, MQ0 &gt;= 4 &amp;&amp; ((MQ0/(1.0*DP)) &gt; 0.1, -cluster 3 -window 10. We ignore the multi-nucleotide polymorphisms, and the loci containing SNP markers must present in at least 90% of individuals. A total of 14,767,700 high-quality SNPs were identified and used in the subsequent analyses.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Phylogenetic relationship of resequenced pistachio</h3><p>We constructed a neighbor-joining tree using a <i>p</i>-distance matrix by TreeBeST (<a href="http://treesoft.sourceforge.net/treebest.shtml">http://treesoft.sourceforge.net/treebest.shtml</a>) with 100 bootstrap replications. Principal component analysis (PCA) was performed using the toolset SNPRelate from the R package. We ran frappe to estimate the genetic ancestry of each sample, specifying a range of 25 hypothetical ancestral populations. The maximum number of interaction was set to 10,000 in the frappe analysis.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Artificial selection analysis</h3><p>We calculated the genome-wide distribution of population fixation statistics <i>F</i><sub>ST</sub> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Weir BS, Cockerham CC. Estimating F-statistics for the analysis of population structure. Evolution. 1984;38:135870." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2071">82</a>] and nucleotide diversity <i></i> and Wattersons estimator <i>w</i> ratios (windows with a number of variants &lt;20 were ignored) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Nei M, Li WH. Mathematical model for studying genetic variation in terms of restriction endonucleases. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 1979;76:526973." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2080">83</a>] for each sliding window with a window size of 50kb and a step size of 25kb. Putative selection targets were extracted with both top 5% of log ratios for <i></i> and <i>F</i><sub>ST</sub>. Our approach was to identify genomic regions with high differentiation between cultivated and wild <i>Pistacia vera</i> (<i>n</i><sub>cultivar</sub>=13, <i>n</i><sub>wild</sub>=14).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">Analysis of genetic introgression</h3><p>We inferred gene flow between the diverged populations using the maximum likelihood method implemented in TreeMix [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Pickrell JK, Pritchard JK. Inference of population splits and mixtures from genome-wide allele frequency data. PLoS Genet. 2012;8:e1002967." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2111">29</a>]. First, we inferred the maximum likelihood (ML) tree with the command -i input -bootstrap -o output. Second, from one to four migration events were gradually added to the ML tree of the five species with command was -i input -bootstrap -k 1000 -m migration events -o output. Genetic introgression was also analyzed by the <i>D</i> statistic (ABBA-BABA test) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Green RE, Krause J, Briggs AW, Maricic T, Stenzel U, Kircher M, Patterson N, Li H, Zhai W, Fritz MH-Y, et al. A draft sequence of the Neandertal genome. Science. 2010;328:71022." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2117">84</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">Recent demographic history inference using ai</h3><p>To uncover the recent demographic history of the cultivated and wild <i>P. vera</i>, we only considered SNPs with more than 40-fold sequencing coverage at the population level in intergenic regions to ensure their neutrality. Missing genotypes were imputed using the program BEAGLE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Browning SR, Browning BL. Rapid and accurate haplotype phasing and missing-data inference for whole-genome association studies by use of localized haplotype clustering. Am J Hum Genet. 2007;81:108497." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2132">85</a>]. After investigating the empirical distributions of the MAFs, haplotypes were inferred for all genotype sites with MAF&gt;0.01. Two divergence models were considered between the two populations of <i>P. vera</i>. The model with the maximum log-likelihood value was chosen as the optimal one.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec31">PSMC analysis</h3><p>Dynamic changes in the effective population size of <i>Pistacia</i> species were inferred using the PSMC program [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Li H, Durbin R. Inference of human population history from individual whole-genome sequences. Nature. 2011;475:4936." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2149">86</a>], with a mutation rate of 7.7e9 and a generation time of 10years [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Parfitt DE, Badenes ML. Phylogeny of the genus Pistacia as determined from analysis of the chloroplastgenome. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 1997;94:798792." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-019-1686-3#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d1768e2152">87</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec32">GO and KEGG enrichment analysis</h3><p>Gene Ontology (GO) enrichment analyses were performed using the DAVID program (<a href="https://david.ncifcrf.gov/">https://david.ncifcrf.gov/</a>) and g: profiler (<a href="https://biit.cs.ut.ee/gprofiler/">https://biit.cs.ut.ee/gprofiler/</a>).</p></div></div></section>
